<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The number of shares of the
Registrant&#146;s Common Stock outstanding as of March&nbsp;28, 2005 was 9,669,250.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">DOCUMENTS&#160; INCORPORATED BY REFERENCE:</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Portions of the Definitive Proxy Statement
for the 2005 Annual Meeting of Shareholders (the &#147;2005 Proxy Statement&#148;) are
incorporated by reference into Part&nbsp;III of this Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K contains
certain forward looking statements.&#160;
Actual results could differ materially from those projected in the
forward looking statements as a result of certain factors, described elsewhere
herein, including but not limited to fluctuations in the market price of gold
and uncertainties regarding the ability of the Joint Venture (as defined below)
to operate profitably.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">PART&nbsp;I</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 1. BUSINESS</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Golden Cycle Gold Corporation was
incorporated under the laws of the State of Colorado on May&nbsp;19, 1972 for
the purpose of acquiring and developing the mining properties (the &#147;Mining
Properties&#148;) of the Golden Cycle Corporation, located in the Cripple Creek
Mining District of Colorado.&#160; Unless the
context otherwise requires, the terms &#147;Registrant&#148; and &#147;Company&#148; as well as &#147;we&#148;,
&#147;us&#148; and &#147;our&#148;, mean Golden Cycle Gold Corporation.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The primary business of the Company has been
its participation in the Cripple Creek&nbsp;&amp; Victor Gold Mining Company (&#147;CC&amp;V&#148;),
a joint venture (the &#147;Joint Venture&#148;) with AngloGold Ashanti (Colorado) Corp.,
formerly Pikes Peak Mining Company (&#147;AngloGold&#148;), a wholly-owned subsidiary of
AngloGold Ashanti North America Inc., which, in turn, is a wholly owned
subsidiary of AngloGold Ashanti Ltd.&#160; The
Joint Venture engages in gold mining activity in the Cripple Creek area of
Colorado.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In addition to its Joint Venture activities,
the Company incorporated Golden Cycle Philippines,&nbsp;Inc. (&#147;GCPI&#148;), a
wholly-owned subsidiary, under the laws of the Philippines on November&nbsp;12,
1996.&#160; GCPI entered into an agreement
with Benguet Corporation, a Philippine mining company, providing for their
joint participation in the exploration, development and production of mining
properties in certain areas of the Philippines.&#160;
All GCPI exploration work has been placed on a standby basis until a
Mineral Profits Sharing Agreement (&#147;MPSA&#148;) is awarded to the claim owner of the
Sagittarius Alpha Realty (&#147;SAR&#148;) claims.&#160;
See &#147;Golden Cycle Philippines,&nbsp;Inc.&#148; for further information
regarding the proposed activities of GCPI in the Philippines.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During January&nbsp;2002, the Company
incorporated Golden Cycle Gold Exploration,&nbsp;Inc., a wholly-owned
subsidiary, to conduct exploration activities for the Company.&#160; As of this date the Company has not funded
Golden Cycle Gold Exploration,&nbsp;Inc.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As of December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company had
3 employees.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Description of Mining Joint Venture</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s interest in the Joint Venture
was received in exchange for the Company&#146;s rights to gold mining properties in
the Cripple Creek Mining District of Colorado.&#160;
The rights and obligations of the parties are covered by an Amended and
Restated Joint Venture Agreement (the &#147;Joint Venture Agreement&#148;) dated and
effective as of January&nbsp;1, 1991, between AngloGold and the Company.&#160; The Joint Venture engages in gold mining
activity in the Cripple Creek area of Colorado and the Company&#146;s participation
in the Joint Venture constitutes its primary business activity.&#160; AngloGold serves as the manager (the &#147;Manager&#148;)
of the Joint Venture.&#160; The Joint Venture&#146;s
principal mining operations are conducted at the Cresson mine, where commercial
production was commenced in the first half of 1995.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture Agreement defines an
Initial Phase that will end when (i)&nbsp;the Initial Loans (defined below)
have been repaid and (ii)&nbsp;Net Proceeds (defined in the Joint Venture
Agreement generally as gross revenues less costs) in the amount of $58 million
have been distributed as follows: 80% to AngloGold and 20% to the Company.&#160; After the Initial Phase, the Joint Venture
will distribute metal in kind in the proportion of 67% to AngloGold and 33% to
the Company.&#160; In addition, the Company
will generally be entitled to receive, in each year during the Initial Phase or
until the mining of ore by the Joint Venture ceases due to the exhaustion of
economically recoverable reserves, whichever occurs first, an annual minimum
distribution of $250,000 (a &#147;Minimum Annual Distribution&#148;).&#160; The first three Minimum Annual Distributions
in 1991, 1992 and 1993 were not deemed to be a distribution of Net Proceeds to
the Company and were not applied against the Company&#146;s share of any Net
Proceeds.&#160; The Minimum Annual
Distributions received on January&nbsp;15, 1994 and thereafter constitute an
advance on Net Proceeds and will be recouped against future shares of Net
Proceeds to the Company.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture Agreement provides that,
during the period from January&nbsp;1, 1991 until the end of the Initial Phase,
all funds required for operations and mine development by the Joint Venture
will be loaned (the &#147;Initial Loans&#148;) to the Joint Venture by either AngloGold
or, if such loans are available at a lower cost than from AngloGold, financial
institutions.&#160; Except for the Minimum
Annual Distributions, the Initial Loans and interest thereon must be repaid
prior to distributions of Net Proceeds to the Joint Venturers.&#160; The audited Joint Venture financial
statements reported that as of December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Joint Venture had
$365.7 million in Initial Loans payable to AngloGold.&#160; After the Initial Phase, the Joint Venturers
will contribute funds in proportion to their respective distributive shares.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture recorded net income of $7.7
million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 compared to net losses of
$0.5 million and $14.3 million for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2003 and December&nbsp;31,
2002, respectively.&#160; There is no
assurance that the Joint Venture will be able to achieve profitability in any
subsequent period or to sustain profitability for an extended period.&#160; The ability of the Joint Venture to sustain
profitability is dependent upon a number of factors beyond the control of the
Joint Venture , including without limitation, the market price of gold, which
is volatile and subject to speculative movement, and the extent of
mineralization in the area controlled by the Joint Venture and the efficiency
of its mining operations.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='3',FILE='C:\JMS\tvalley\05-3673-1\task380169\3673-1-ba-01.htm',USER='tvalley',CD='Mar 31 11:36 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Whether future gold prices and the results of
the Joint Venture&#146;s operations will reach and maintain a level necessary to
repay the Initial Loans, complete the Initial Phase, and thereafter generate
net income cannot be assured.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture completed construction of
the required infrastructure for the Cresson Mine and began mining operations in
1995, with the first Cresson Mine gold pour occurring on February&nbsp;14,
1995.&#160; In 1996, the Joint Venture
completed its first full year of Cresson Mine operations.&#160; The development of the East and North Cresson
mines began during the second quarter of 1999.&#160;
The Joint Venture began construction of expanded facilities during early
2002, completing the new truck shop, crushing facility, expanded process
facility, and expanded valley leach facility by September&nbsp;2003.&#160; The last step in the mine expansion, a $15.5
million expansion of the valley fill leach facility, was completed during the
fall of 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2004 Operational Highlights</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As the Joint Venture&#146;s Manager, AngloGold
provides the Company with detailed information on the activities and operations
of the Joint Venture.&#160; The following
description of the Joint Venture&#146;s operation is derived from information made
available by the Manager, upon whom reliance is placed.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Production</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 2004 Joint Venture gold production was
329,029 troy ounces (approximately 94% of budget) compared to 283,886 troy
ounces of gold (83% of budget) produced during 2003.&#160; CC&amp;V has corrected most of the leach pad
chemistry problems previously reported and is experiencing improved
recoveries.&#160; CC&amp;V is monitoring and
working to improve leach pad chemistry on a daily basis.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CC&amp;V appears to have overcome its truck
capacity problems, chiefly through improved maintenance.&#160; CC&amp;V mined 58.3 million tons of material
during the year (the expansion plan budgeted rate is 58 million tons a year),
including 20.3 million tons of ore and 38 million tons of waste.&#160;&#160; CC&amp;V also moved 1.3 million tons of
stockpiled ore to the crusher for a total of 59.6 million tons moved.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The new primary crusher operated at plant
capacity during the year, crushing 20.1 million tons during the year versus a
budget of 20 million tons.&#160; Ore placed on
the valley leach facility averaged 0.0245 troy ounces per ton, containing an
estimated 492,943 troy ounces of gold (an estimated 355,950 recoverable ounces
of gold).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Revenue and Costs</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture sold approximately 331,299
troy ounces of gold at an average price of $409.52 per ounce producing total
metal sale revenues of approximately $135.7 million.&#160; The Joint Venture cash production costs for
2004 were approximately $256 per troy ounce compared to $198.9 per troy ounce
during 2003 and a budget of $225.34 per troy ounce.&#160; The main reason for the higher cost per ounce
in 2004 compared to the budgeted cost per ounce was the reduced number of
ounces produced (94% of budget) and increased variable costs such as diesel
fuel.&#160; The Joint Venture had total operating
costs of $104.4 million, including depreciation, depletion and amortization
(DD&amp;A) of $30.7 million, and expensed exploration</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">4</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

</div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">of approximately $1.4 million for the year, compared to $85.1 million,
$25.8 million and $2.8 million comparatively for the year ended 2003.&#160; Interest expense on the Initial Loans was
approximately $23.8 million ($22.4 million in the year 2003).&#160; The Company did receive the Minimum Annual Distribution
of $250,000, which will be recouped from future shares of Net Proceeds to the
Company.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Ore Reserves and Non-reserve Mineralization</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture is conducting continuing
exploration and engineering feasibility work concerning future operations.&#160; These activities will serve to direct future
exploration drilling programs as well as future development and project
planning as part of its determination of the Joint Venture reserves.&#160; The main objective of CC&amp;V&#146;s continuing
exploration program for 2004 was to delineate the boundaries of two areas of
mineralization in the Wild Horse Extension area and to increase the drill
information available within areas which have previously indicated existing
mineralization.&#160; The decrease in current
reserves is due to depletion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CC&amp;V currently controls over 85% of the
patented claims within the district and 100% of the land within the year-end
2004 Ore Reserve Estimate.&#160; All gold ore
reserves and mineral resources are stated at 100% ownership basis although
portions of the ore reserves are subject to third party royalties which vary
according to individual agreements with the underlying property owner.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each year CC&amp;V models its gold ore
reserves to incorporate the results of its exploration program, new geologic
information, revised metallurgical recoveries, revised gold price, new geotechnical
data, new pit designs, new operating costs and/or allowances for 2004
depletion.&#160; The ore reserves and mineral
resources shown for 2004 were modeled using a $375 gold price and a 0.007 ounce
per ton (opt) recoverable cutoff grade.&#160;
A total of 252,654 feet of additional drilling was added (308 drill
holes), and all geotechnical data remains as reported at year end 2003.&#160; Resources remain restricted to a $425
Lerchs-Grossmann shell envelope around the reserve pits.&#160; The geostatistical modeling procedures used
by the Manager in computing the ore reserves have been reviewed by independent
consultants (Independent Mining Consultants,&nbsp;Inc., Mine Reserve Associates,&nbsp;Inc.,
Mineral Resource Development Associates,&nbsp;Inc., and Mine Development
Associates,&nbsp;Inc.) over previous years, and conform to industry
standards.&#160; The ore reserves are shown on
the table below:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Unaudited

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left">

</font></i></div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Note:&#160;
</font>The tonnage is shown in short tons.</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">*&#160;&#160;&#160; These
gold reserve figures were estimated based on a $375 per troy ounce gold price
for all district deposits, and are subject to various royalties.&#160; There can be no assurance, however, that the
Joint Venture can earn a profit when the market price of gold equals or exceeds
the gold price used in estimating those reserves.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">**&#160;
</font>Recoverability of contained ounces is based on heap leaching and
metallurgical testing.&#160; Recoverability
rates vary by ore type.&#160; The recoverable
ounces shown are based on weight proportion metallurgical averages for all
deposits.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The above estimates are based upon drill data
and are a combination of &#147;proven&#148; and &#147;probable&#148; reserves.&#160; The classifications of &#147;proven&#148; and &#147;probable&#148;
are taken from the Securities and Exchange Commission&#146;s Industry Guide 7, which
defines the terms as follows.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Proven (Measured) Reserves</font></i>.&#160; Reserves for which (a)&nbsp;quantity is
computed from dimensions revealed in outcrops, trenches, workings or drill
holes; grade and/or quality are computed from the results of detailed sampling
and (b)&nbsp;the sites for inspection, sampling and measurement are spaced so
closely and the geologic character is so well defined that the size, shape,
depth and mineral content of reserves are well established.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Probable (Indicated) Reserves</font></i>.&#160; Reserves for which quantity and grade and/or
quality are computed from information similar to that used for proven
(measured) reserves, but the sites for inspection, sampling, and measurement
are farther apart or are otherwise less adequately spaced.&#160; The degree of assurance, although lower than
that for proven (measured) reserves, is high enough to assume continuity
between points of observation.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The ore reserve figures set forth above are
estimates and no assurance can be given that any particular level of recovery
of gold from ore reserves will in fact be realized.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The focus of the Joint Venture&#146;s 2005 exploration
program is to develop additional metallurgical information in mineral resource
areas to enable it to change the classification of a portion of its non-reserve
mineral resources to mineral reserve ounces of gold.&#160; It expects to achieve this goal through
additional infill drilling, geotech and metallurgical drilling and studies and
mining studies.&#160; Further, the Joint
Venture is exploring a new area on a widely- spaced drill hole basis with the
objective of defining a mineral resource in the area.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Environmental Reclamation</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:1.0in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CC&amp;V has developed an effective
environmental protection and reclamation plan for this high-altitude, semiarid,
cold-weather, year-round leaching environment.&#160;
Reclamation has continued since 1992 to support post mining land use for
wild life, including elk.&#160; Work continued
in 2004 on the detoxification of the Victor leach pad with a view to its
eventual closure and final reclamation.&#160;
Although the Victor leach pad has been detoxified to less than free
cyanide standards for detoxification, its nitrates level remain elevated. The
Joint Venture has secured total financial warranties of approximately $45
million to insure its success in completing the final reclamation of the entire
property.&#160; Ongoing compliance with
federal and state regulations includes seismic, fugitive dust, and noise
monitoring for the</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></i></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='6',FILE='C:\JMS\tvalley\05-3673-1\task380169\3673-1-ba-01.htm',USER='tvalley',CD='Mar 31 11:36 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">operation&#146;s meeting applicable standards for ground and surface water;
monitoring rain and snow fall, water and air emissions.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Employment</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">AngloGold provides the work force required by
the Joint Venture, which has no employees.&#160;
AngloGold employment related to the Joint Venture increased to 316 at December&nbsp;31,
2004, from 304 at December&nbsp;31, 2003.&#160;
The increase in employment was a result of completing the mine
expansion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Governmental Regulation</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Like all mining operations in the United
States, the Joint Venture is subject to a multitude of environmental laws and
regulations promulgated by federal, state and local governments including, but
not limited to, the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation and
Liability Act (&#147;CERCLA&#148;);&#160; the Clean Air
Act (&#147;CAA&#148;); the Clean Water Act (&#147;CWA&#148;); the Hazardous Materials
Transportation Act (&#147;HMTA&#148;); the Toxic Substances Control Act (&#147;TSCA&#148;);
Resource Conservation and Recovery Act (&#147;RCRA&#148;) and the Colorado Mined Land
Reclamation Act.&#160; The Joint Venture&#146;s
operations are subject to comprehensive regulation by the United States
Environmental Protection Agency (&#147;EPA&#148;), the United States Mine Safety and
Health Administration (&#147;MSHA&#148;) and other state and local agencies.&#160; Failure to comply with applicable laws,
regulations and permits can result in injunctive action, damages and civil and
criminal penalties.&#160; If the Joint Venture
expands or changes its existing operations or proposes new operations, it may
be required to obtain additional or amended permits or authorizations.&#160; In particular, CERCLA, commonly called the &#147;Superfund
Act&#148;, contains stringent reporting requirements for the release or disposal of
hazardous substances, with substantial fines for noncompliance.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Certain solid and hazardous wastes from
mining and mineral processing operations are temporarily exempt from regulation
under RCRA.&#160; The EPA is currently
considering the promulgation of a special set of rules&nbsp;to regulate mining
wastes under RCRA, but those may be delayed pending anticipated Congressional
re-authorization and revision of RCRA.&#160;
The effect of any future regulation on the Joint Venture&#146;s operations
cannot be determined until the legislative process is completed and new rules&nbsp;are
issued.&#160; However, it is assumed that
regulations may have a significant impact on operations of all mining companies
and increase the costs of those operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Although the Manager expects that compliance
with federal, state and local environmental and land use laws and regulations
will continue to require significant future outlays of resources, it is not
possible to say with any certainty what impact such compliance may have on the
Joint Venture&#146;s future capital expenditures or earnings.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Distribution of Proceeds and Other Financial
Aspects</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture made payments of the
Minimum Annual Distribution of $250,000 to the Company on June&nbsp;13, 1991, January&nbsp;15,
1992, and January&nbsp;15 of each subsequent year, to and including January&nbsp;15,
2005.&#160; Subsequent payments of the same
amount are scheduled to be made on January&nbsp;15th of each year until the
conclusion of the Initial Phase, as defined in the Joint Venture Agreement, or
until the completion of mining.&#160; The
payments made on</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></i></div>

</div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">January&nbsp;15, 1994 and subsequent annual payments of $250,000
constitute an advance on Net Proceeds and will be recouped by the Manager
against future distributions of net proceeds.&#160;
After recovery by the Manager of these advances, if the Company&#146;s share
(20% in the Initial Phase) of Net Proceeds exceeds the applicable Minimum
Annual Distribution after recouping any advanced distributions, the larger
amount will be distributed to the Company.&#160;
The Joint Venture recorded net income of $7.7 million for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company accounts for its investment in
the Joint Venture on the equity method.&#160;
Joint Venture distributions in excess of the investment carrying value
are recorded as income.&#160; During 1992, the
Company&#146;s share of Joint Venture losses exceeded the remaining carrying value
of the investment and, accordingly, the investment was reduced to zero.&#160; The Company does not record its share of
Joint Venture losses incurred subsequent to the reduction of its investment
balance to zero.&#160; The Company believes
that its liability for loss is limited to its loss of its equity in the Joint
Venture.&#160; To the extent the Joint Venture
is subsequently profitable, the Company will not record its share of equity
income until the cumulative amount of previously unrecorded Joint Venture
losses has been recouped.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As a result of the reduction of the Joint
Venture investment carrying value to zero during 1992, the Company has not
recorded its share of the Joint Venture net income for the 2004 period,
$1,538,400, nor its share of the Joint Venture&#146;s net loss for the 2003 period
($93,800) or 2002 period ($2,863,600).&#160;
The Company will not record its share of any future Joint Venture net
income unless and until the balance of the Company&#146;s accumulated unrecorded
losses from the Joint Venture ($17,480,058 as of December&nbsp;31, 2004) are
recovered.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">GOLDEN CYCLE PHILIPPINES, INC. (GCPI)</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">GCPI and its exploration activities were
placed into a standby status in January&nbsp;1999 for the reasons stated below.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">GCPI Background</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In January&nbsp;1997, GCPI signed a
comprehensive exploration agreement (the &#147;BGA Agreement&#148;) with Benguet
Corporation (&#147;Benguet&#148;), which provided that all costs and participation will
be shared 50/50 by the parties.&#160; In October&nbsp;1997,
the two companies signed the First Supplemental Agreement to the BGA Agreement,
which added 1,050 acres of mineral claims held by Benguet to the BGA.&#160; Under the terms of this supplemental agreement,
GCPI will earn a 50% interest in these claims in exchange for funding the first
$250,000 (about 10 million Philippine pesos) of exploration work.&#160; The claim area lies immediately south of the
historic Masara and Hijo gold mines in the Philippines and just north of
Benguet&#146;s Kingking copper/gold deposit.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">First Supplemental Agreement to the BGA</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Phase I of the exploration effort on the five
Sagittarius Alpha Realty (&#147;SAR&#148;) claims was completed in May&nbsp;1998.&#160; This effort consisted of geological mapping,
grid soil sampling and analysis, and stream sediment and water analysis.&#160; This work indicates the presence of sizable
areas interpreted to be anomalous gold concentrations.&#160; These must be further tested through
trenching, tunneling and drilling to properly evaluate the gold potential.&#160; The Phase II</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">8</font></p>

</font></i></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">exploration could not be carried out as the old leased claims have not
as of this date been awarded a Mineral Production Sharing Agreement (&#147;MPSA&#148;) as
required by the 1995 Philippine Mining Law. Thus, all work on this project has
been placed on a standby basis until the MPSA is awarded to Benguet, as claim
owner.&#160; Benguet has not applied for an
MPSA as of March&nbsp;2005.&#160; The Company
expects to expend approximately $5,000 during 2005 to maintain GCPI on a
standby status.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">OTHER OPPORTUNITIES</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During 2001 the Company acquired two claim
groups in Nevada: the Table Top and the Illipah gold prospects.&#160; During first quarter 2002 the Company
incorporated a wholly owned subsidiary, Golden Cycle Gold Exploration,&nbsp;Inc.
(&#147;GCX&#148;), to independently direct the exploration efforts for these claim
groups.&#160; As of this report, the Company
has not yet funded GCX.&#160; Finally, the
Company has an on-going exploration program in southwest Colorado.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Table Top</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Table Top claim group consists of 38
twenty acre claims and lies within the Basin and Range province of
north-central Nevada, which over the past forty years has become one of the
world&#146;s premier gold producing regions.&#160;
The Table Top property can be interpreted to lie within the &#147;Midas&#148; gold
bearing zone striking northeast across Nevada, and also as a part of a
north-south trend containing the Sleeper Mine, Sandman, Florida Canyon,
Rochester and Relief Canyon.&#160; The
property is located ten miles west of Winnemucca, Nevada.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Table Top claims cover a brecciated and
silicified sediment that is poorly exposed and has only been unsystematically
explored and partially drill tested in the past.&#160; The key gold mineralized feature on the property
is a hydrothermal breccia, which contains anomalous gold, arsenic, antimony and
mercury.&#160; Goldfields Mining Corporation
first staked the Table Top property in 1986 while conducting surface
exploration for an open pit type operation.&#160;
A limited rock chip sampling and reverse circulation drilling program
indicated the presence of a gold mineralized system.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s intended exploration target
will be the discovery of a high grade mineralized gold vein system at depth, to
be developed by a phased exploration program.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Illipah</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s Board of Directors has approved
a budget to drill test the Illipah claim groups located in White Pine County,
Nevada.&#160; This gold project is situated in
eastern Nevada at the southern extension of the Carlin Trend that contains the
largest accumulation of gold deposits in North America.&#160; The Company&#146;s controls 191 unpatented lode,
mining claims (approximately 3800 acres) over a six-mile strike length that
contains favorable stratigraphic and structural environments for the discovery
of a significant gold deposit.&#160; The
property is subject to advance royalty payments and a 2% Net Smelter Return (&#147;NSR&#148;)
royalty on all mineral production.&#160; An
NSR is a royalty, usually a percent, of smelter production less certain
allowable costs such as smelting and transportation to the smelter.&#160; The NSR royalty is reduced to 1% if
$2,000,000 in advance royalties is paid.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Past production from the immediate area of
Illipah is 37,000 ounces of gold from an</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></i></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">open pit mined in the late 1980&#146;s and early 1990&#146;s.&#160; The ore was processed using heap leach
technology.&#160; This gold mineralization is
envisioned as a surface gold anomaly that indicates there is a strong
possibility of high-grade gold mineralization at depth near favorable
stratigraphic contacts and structures.&#160;
The geological similarities between Illipah and Newmont&#146;s Rain Deposit
(the &#147;Rain Deposit&#148;) located 65 miles north-northwest are striking.&#160; The Rain Deposit originally was mined as an
open-pit, but is currently being mined underground.&#160; The reported resource potential is 2 million
ounces of gold and the average grade 0.40 oz/troy Au.&#160; An underground target similar to the Rain
Deposit is the concept being tested by the approved drill program that Golden
Cycle will undertake in the spring of 2005.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The recommended drill program for Illipah
consists of eight reverse circulation drill holes which will be angled to
approximate perpendicular to the envisioned structures.&#160; The holes are designed to test the favorable
stratigraphic horizons and structural intersections at depth beneath gold
anomalies on the surface.&#160; The depths of
the drill holes will range from 800 to 1500 feet.&#160; A budget of approximately $259,000 will fund
the drilling, assaying of samples, personnel, expenses, application and filing
for exploration permit and necessary bonding.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Colorado</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A continuing exploration effort is underway
in the Company&#146;s home state of Colorado, which the Company believes is
currently being overlooked by both junior and major mining companies.&#160; This exploration is focused on a particular
area in southwest Colorado where the Company has developed a geologic concept
indicating the possibility of an exploration target which meets the Company&#146;s
criterion.&#160; During 2005, the Company will
complete a regional study of the target area, including satellite imagery which
it began in 2004, with the objective of narrowing the target area.&#160; The Company is also continuing its selective
search in western Colorado for additional mineral prospects to undertake during
2005.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM
2.&#160; PROPERTIES</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">MINING, OIL AND GAS, AND WATER RIGHTS</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mining Properties</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture mining properties consist
of owned, leased and optioned mining claims and other land covering more than
4,800 acres of patented mining claims in and around the Cripple Creek Mining
District of Teller County, Colorado and include most of the principal
formerly-producing mines of the Cripple Creek district.&#160; The majority of the above acreage was
contributed by the Company to the Joint Venture.&#160; Subsequently, the Joint Venture has
purchased, leased and optioned additional acreage, and continues to do so as
opportunity arises to complete the consolidation of the district.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture mining properties are
situated on the west flank of Pikes Peak, about 20 air miles west of Colorado
Springs and 65 air miles south of Denver.&#160;
The area is accessible by paved highway and supplied by requisite
utilities.&#160; The elevation of the
properties averages slightly over 10,000 feet above sea level.&#160; Snow accumulations are generally light and do
not materially interfere with access to the property.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">10</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To a great extent, the Joint Venture mining
properties lie within the boundary of a geological entity known as a caldera or
&#147;volcanic subsidence basin&#148; (the &#147;Basin&#148;).&#160;
The Basin is of rudimentary elliptical outline, with its long axis
trending in a northwesterly direction.&#160;
It has a length of about 4-1/2 miles and a width of about 2-1/2 miles,
covering some 5,000 acres at the ground surface.&#160; The area of the Basin gradually narrows with
depth.&#160; The bulk of the historical
Cripple Creek gold production was from the underground mines within the Basin,
with the major mines located in the southern portion of the Basin.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">From the inception of production in 1891
until the suspension of operations in 1960, the Cripple Creek Mining District
was the major gold mining district in the United States.&#160; It is estimated that approximately 21 million
ounces of gold were produced in this period, principally from mines later
contributed to the Joint Venture by Golden Cycle Gold Corporation.&#160; The Joint Venture, including a number of
joint venture partners, has added about 2.5 million troy ounces of gold
production to this total during the period 1985 through 2004.&#160; The Joint Venture mining properties include
most of the principal formerly producing mines in the Cripple Creek district,
including the Ajax, Cresson, Portland, Independence, Vindicator and Golden
Cycle.&#160; Because of the age of many of the
mines and the fact that mining operations throughout the Basin declined and
were suspended more than thirty years ago, the existing mine shafts and
workings are unsuitable for current operation without substantial
rehabilitation.&#160; The Joint Venture is not
currently and does not anticipate, operating underground.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Oil and Gas Mineral Rights</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The oil and gas properties of the Company are
comprised of approximately 7,300 acres of mineral rights in the Penrose Area of
Fremont County, Colorado.&#160; There is no
evidence of successful oil and gas development nearby, with the exception of
the Florence, Colorado area.&#160; Florence
was the site of the first producing wells in Colorado in the 1860&#146;s and the
area is still producing on a limited scale today.&#160; Several years ago, interest was shown in
leasing very large acreages of state land about 50 to70 miles east of the
Company&#146;s land.&#160; No development of that
area is visible at this time, nor is it expected in the forseeable future.&#160; The oil and gas properties have no carrying
value for balance sheet purposes.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 3.&#160;
LEGAL PROCEEDINGS</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As previously reported, the Sierra Club and
Mineral Policy Center filed two complaints in U.S. District Court for the
District of Colorado against CC&amp;V and its Joint Venture partners, including
the Company, alleging certain violations of the CWA.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;text-indent:-.25in;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
first ten Causes of Action in the first of these two cases allege un-permitted
discharges of pollutants into Fourmile Creek and from the Roosevelt Tunnel into
Cripple Creek, and discharges of pollutants exceeding permitted amounts from
the Carlton Tunnel and Arequa Gulch outfalls; the eleventh and twelfth causes
of action in that case concern a discharge permit issued by the Colorado Water
Quality Control Division in 1996 for an outfall in Arequa Gulch.&#160; A pre-trial conference was held on March&nbsp;25,
2005, in this case, and it</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">11</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></i></div>

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='11',FILE='C:\JMS\tvalley\05-3673-1\task380169\3673-1-ba-01.htm',USER='tvalley',CD='Mar 31 11:36 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">should be
ready by mid-summer for trial, though no trial date has yet been set.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;text-indent:-.25in;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
second of these two cases relates to seeps asserted to be point-source
discharges of Cresson Project drainage from the Moffat Tunnel Cribbing Wall and
the Squaw Gulch Pond to Cripple Creek and a tributary thereto in Squaw
Gulch.&#160; Plantiffs assert and Defendants
deny that the law requires a permit for these seeps.&#160; This case was set for trial on April&nbsp;12,
2005, but that setting was vacated and the two cases consolidated for trial on
a date not yet set.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 65.25pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;text-indent:-20.25pt;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Management is contesting both of these cases,
and is coordinating its own efforts with those of the owner and operator,
CC&amp;V, and the majority owners thereof, AngloGold North America,&nbsp;Inc.,
and AngloGold Colorado Corp.&#160; The Company
is neither the owner nor operator and its interest is limited to its minority
interest in CC&amp;V.&#160; Therefore, the
likelihood of an unfavorable outcome to the Company cannot be evaluated, and no
estimate can be made of the amount or range of potential loss, if any, which
might result either to the Company or to its interest in CC&amp;V.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The suit pending at the end of 2003 in
Madison County, Illinois, was recently dismissed on stipulation.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company expended approximately $17,000
and $12,500 during the years 2004 and 2003, respectively, defending against
these suits.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 4.&#160;
SUBMISSION OF MATTERS TO A VOTE OF SECURITY HOLDERS</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company did not submit any matters to a
vote of security holders during the fourth quarter of 2004.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">12</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s Common Stock has been listed
and traded on the Pacific Exchange since 1987 (except during the period from July&nbsp;6,
1994 to August&nbsp;30, 1994), and from July&nbsp;1, 1983 until June&nbsp;30,
1992 was quoted on NASDAQ.&#160; The Company&#146;s
trading symbol is GCGC on the Pacific Exchange.&#160;
The following table shows the high and low bid price per share on the
Pacific Exchange, or the Over the Counter market, for each calendar quarter
since January&nbsp;1, 2003.&#160; All stock
prices have been adjusted to reflect the five for one stock split July&nbsp;2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Holders of the Company&#146;s Common Stock</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The number of holders of record of the
Company&#146;s Common Stock as of March&nbsp;28, 2005 was 804.&#160; The number of beneficial owners for whom
shares are held in &#147;street name&#148; as of March&nbsp;28, 2005 is believed to be
more than 500.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Dividends</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has not paid any dividends.&#160; The Company effected a five-for-one stock
split effective July&nbsp;2004 following shareholder approval of an increase in
the authorized shares of the Company&#146;s Common Stock from 3.5 million to 100
million at the 2004 annual meeting of shareholders.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Equity Compensation Plans</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following table shows information for all
equity compensation plans:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160;(2)&nbsp; The Joint Venture
recorded net income of $7.7 million for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004,
and net losses of $0.5 million and $14.3 million for the years ended December&nbsp;31,
2003 and 2002, respectively.&#160; The Company
has not recorded its share of the Joint Venture net income for the 2004 period
($1,538,400) nor its share of the Joint Venture&#146;s net loss for the 2003 period
($93,800) or 2002 period ($2,863,600) because its Joint Venture investment
balance was reduced to zero in 1992.&#160; The
Company will not record its share of any future Joint Venture net income until
and unless the balance of the Company&#146;s accumulated unrecorded losses from the
Joint Venture ($17,480,058 as of December&nbsp;31, 2004) are recovered.&#160; See Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis
below, and Notes to the consolidated financial statements.</font></p>

<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">ITEM 7.&#160;
MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS
OF OPERATION</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Overview</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our financial statements consolidate the
operations of our wholly-owned subsidiary, Golden Cycle Philippines,&nbsp;Inc.
with those of Golden Cycle Gold Corporation.&#160;
Golden Cycle Philippines,&nbsp;Inc. has minimal costs and assets and
Golden Cycle Gold Exploration,&nbsp;Inc. had no operations or assets during the
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Currently, our primary mining investment and
source of cash flows is our 33% interest in the CC&amp;V Joint Venture.&#160; The Joint Venture engages in gold mining
activity in the Cripple Creek area of Colorado.&#160;
The Company&#146;s Joint Venture co-venturer is AngloGold.&#160; In addition to our interest in the Joint
Venture, we own three gold mineral prospects which we are not actively
exploring at present.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our rights and obligations relating to our
Joint Venture interest are governed by the Joint Venture Agreement.&#160; The Joint Venture is currently, and for the
foreseeable future will be, operating in the Initial Phase, as defined in the
Joint Venture Agreement.&#160; In accordance
with the Joint Venture Agreement, AngloGold manages the Joint Venture and is
required to finance all operations and capital expenditures during the Initial
Phase.&#160; See &#147;Description of Mining Joint
Venture&#148; above.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Liquidity and Capital Resources</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our working capital was $1,558,000 at December&nbsp;31,
2004 compared to $1,778,000 at December&nbsp;31, 2003.&#160; Cash used in operations was $333,000 in 2004
compared to $300,000 during 2003.&#160; The
increase in cash used in operations during 2004 was primarily due to the
increased general and administrative expenses during the 2004 period.&#160; Working capital decreased by approximately
$220,000 at December&nbsp;31, 2004 compared to December&nbsp;31, 2003 primarily
due to net losses in the 2004 period offset by approximately $98,000 in
proceeds from the exercise of stock options during the year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For 2005, the Company has budgeted
approximately $259,000 for the initial exploration program for its Illipah gold
exploration project.&#160; Exploration permits
have been obtained for exploration drilling on property beyond the drill holes
in the initial exploration budget.&#160; If
the initial exploration proves successful, the Company may elect to accelerate
exploration on the property and has the exploration permits to move rapidly
into phase two exploration drilling.&#160;
Should the Company elect to accelerate the exploration program, it is
likely that the Company will have to raise additional capital to finance the
acceleration.&#160; At this time, the
likelihood that the Company will be able raise additional capital when
required, and the cost of raising such additional capital is unknown.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">15</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='15',FILE='C:\JMS\tvalley\05-3673-1\task380169\3673-1-ba-01.htm',USER='tvalley',CD='Mar 31 11:36 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company completed the sale of certain
Johnson Ditch Water Rights it owned in Fremont County, Colorado to the City of
Cripple Creek on December&nbsp;31, 2003, for $679,098 in the form of a
receivable which resulted in a $546,418 gain.&#160;
The total revenue to the Company from sale of this Water Right was
$991,598, which amount includes the $312,500 which was received by the Company
when a portion of the sale to the City of Cripple Creek closed on December&nbsp;31,
1996.&#160; The Company received payment in
full from the City of Cripple Creek on January&nbsp;7, 2002.&#160; The Company does not have any further Water
Rights.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">We believe that the Company&#146;s working
capital, augmented by the Minimum Annual Distribution from the joint venture,
is adequate to support operations at the current level for the coming year,
barring unforeseen events.&#160; We anticipate
that our Philippine subsidiary will hold all work on a standby basis until the
MPSA is awarded to the claim owner.&#160; If
opportunities to economically pursue or expand Philippine, Nevada, Colorado
operations, or any other opportunity discussed above (see Item 1, Other
Opportunities) are available, and we elect to pursue them, additional working
capital may also be required.&#160; It is possible
that the Company will elect to expand the Illipah exploration program which
will require additional capital.&#160; There
is no assurance that we will be able to obtain such additional capital, if
required, or that such capital would be available to the Company on terms that
would be acceptable.&#160; Furthermore, if we
were to commence such operations, it is not presently known when or if a
positive cash flow could be derived from the operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Results of Operations</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2004 vs 2003</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">We recorded net loss of approximately
$322,000 for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 compared to a net profit for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003 of approximately $224,000.&#160; The difference between the net loss in 2004
compared to the net profit in 2003 was primarily the absence of the gain on the
one time sale of Water Rights in 2003 (see above).&#160; Each year the carrying costs of the Illipah
claim group increase as have most of the general and administrative costs of
doing business.&#160; During the past year,
the cost of compliance with the provisions of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002
also significantly increased the Company&#146;s administrative costs, particularly
its legal expenses.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2003 vs 2002</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">We achieved a net profit of approximately
$224,000 for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003 compared to a net loss for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2002 of approximately $223,000.&#160; The positive results for 2003 were the result
of the completion of the one time sale of our Water Rights to the City of
Cripple Creek which resulted in approximately a $540,000 gain.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">We account for our investment in the Joint
Venture on the equity method.&#160; Joint
Venture distributions in excess of the investment carrying value are recorded
as revenue, as we are not required to finance the Joint Venture&#146;s operating
losses or capital expenditures.&#160;
Correspondingly, we have not recorded our share of Joint Venture income
or losses incurred subsequent to the reduction of the Company&#146;s Joint Venture
investment balance to zero in 1992.&#160; We
will not record our share of equity income until the cumulative amount of</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">16</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">previously unrecorded Joint Venture losses has been recouped.&#160; As of December&nbsp;31, 2004, the Company&#146;s
accumulated unrecorded losses from the Joint Venture are $17,480,058.&#160; At the current prevailing price of gold we do
not expect distributions from the Joint Venture in excess of the Minimum Annual
Distribution ($250,000 per year) for several years.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Joint Venture recorded net income for the
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 of approximately $7.7 million compared to net
losses of $0.5 million, and $14.3 million for the years ended December&nbsp;31,
2003 and 2002, respectively.&#160; The primary
reason for the Joint Venture&#146;s improved performance in both 2004 and 2003 over
the previous years&#146; performance was the increase in the prevailing price for
gold bullion during each year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>
